\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
\begin{DoxyVerb}A multi-level, or hierarchical, index object for pandas objects.

Parameters
----------
levels : sequence of arrays
    The unique labels for each level.
codes : sequence of arrays
    Integers for each level designating which label at each location.
sortorder : optional int
    Level of sortedness (must be lexicographically sorted by that
    level).
names : optional sequence of objects
    Names for each of the index levels. (name is accepted for compat).
copy : bool, default False
    Copy the meta-data.
verify_integrity : bool, default True
    Check that the levels/codes are consistent and valid.

Attributes
----------
names
levels
codes
nlevels
levshape
dtypes

Methods
-------
from_arrays
from_tuples
from_product
from_frame
set_levels
set_codes
to_frame
to_flat_index
sortlevel
droplevel
swaplevel
reorder_levels
remove_unused_levels
get_level_values
get_indexer
get_loc
get_locs
get_loc_level
drop

See Also
--------
MultiIndex.from_arrays  : Convert list of arrays to MultiIndex.
MultiIndex.from_product : Create a MultiIndex from the cartesian product
                          of iterables.
MultiIndex.from_tuples  : Convert list of tuples to a MultiIndex.
MultiIndex.from_frame   : Make a MultiIndex from a DataFrame.
Index : The base pandas Index type.

Notes
-----
See the `user guide
<https://pandas.pydata.org/pandas-docs/stable/user_guide/advanced.html>`__
for more.

Examples
--------
A new ``MultiIndex`` is typically constructed using one of the helper
methods :meth:`MultiIndex.from_arrays`, :meth:`MultiIndex.from_product`
and :meth:`MultiIndex.from_tuples`. For example (using ``.from_arrays``):

>>> arrays = [[1, 1, 2, 2], ['red', 'blue', 'red', 'blue']]
>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays(arrays, names=('number', 'color'))
MultiIndex([(1,  'red'),
            (1, 'blue'),
            (2,  'red'),
            (2, 'blue')],
           names=['number', 'color'])

See further examples for how to construct a MultiIndex in the doc strings
of the mentioned helper methods.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a0ae20377508cd6142bce775ec5727924}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!\_is\_lexsorted@{\_is\_lexsorted}}
\index{\_is\_lexsorted@{\_is\_lexsorted}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\_is\_lexsorted()}{\_is\_lexsorted()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a0ae20377508cd6142bce775ec5727924} 
 bool pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+\_\+is\+\_\+lexsorted (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return True if the codes are lexicographically sorted.

Returns
-------
bool

Examples
--------
In the below examples, the first level of the MultiIndex is sorted because
a<b<c, so there is no need to look at the next level.

>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([['a', 'b', 'c'],
...                            ['d', 'e', 'f']])._is_lexsorted()
True
>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([['a', 'b', 'c'],
...                            ['d', 'f', 'e']])._is_lexsorted()
True

In case there is a tie, the lexicographical sorting looks
at the next level of the MultiIndex.

>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([[0, 1, 1], ['a', 'b', 'c']])._is_lexsorted()
True
>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([[0, 1, 1], ['a', 'c', 'b']])._is_lexsorted()
False
>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([['a', 'a', 'b', 'b'],
...                            ['aa', 'bb', 'aa', 'bb']])._is_lexsorted()
True
>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([['a', 'a', 'b', 'b'],
...                            ['bb', 'aa', 'aa', 'bb']])._is_lexsorted()
False
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{multi_8py_source_l01985}{1985}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{multi_8py_source}{multi.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_aaa7415ded23a2118e9c20f3acfa664c1}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!\_set\_names@{\_set\_names}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\_set\_names()}{\_set\_names()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_aaa7415ded23a2118e9c20f3acfa664c1} 
pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+\_\+set\+\_\+names (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{names}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{}]{level}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{bool }]{validate}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Set new names on index. Each name has to be a hashable type.

Parameters
----------
values : str or sequence
    name(s) to set
level : int, level name, or sequence of int/level names (default None)
    If the index is a MultiIndex (hierarchical), level(s) to set (None
    for all levels).  Otherwise level must be None
validate : bool, default True
    validate that the names match level lengths

Raises
------
TypeError if each name is not hashable.

Notes
-----
sets names on levels. WARNING: mutates!

Note that you generally want to set this *after* changing levels, so
that it only acts on copies
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a442f78f82f2de2644002cc55907715ea}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!\_sort\_levels\_monotonic@{\_sort\_levels\_monotonic}}
\index{\_sort\_levels\_monotonic@{\_sort\_levels\_monotonic}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\_sort\_levels\_monotonic()}{\_sort\_levels\_monotonic()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a442f78f82f2de2644002cc55907715ea} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+\_\+sort\+\_\+levels\+\_\+monotonic (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{bool }]{raise\+\_\+if\+\_\+incomparable}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}This is an *internal* function.

Create a new MultiIndex from the current to monotonically sorted
items IN the levels. This does not actually make the entire MultiIndex
monotonic, JUST the levels.

The resulting MultiIndex will have the same outward
appearance, meaning the same .values and ordering. It will also
be .equals() to the original.

Returns
-------
MultiIndex

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex(levels=[['a', 'b'], ['bb', 'aa']],
...                    codes=[[0, 0, 1, 1], [0, 1, 0, 1]])
>>> mi
MultiIndex([('a', 'bb'),
            ('a', 'aa'),
            ('b', 'bb'),
            ('b', 'aa')],
           )

>>> mi.sort_values()
MultiIndex([('a', 'aa'),
            ('a', 'bb'),
            ('b', 'aa'),
            ('b', 'bb')],
           )
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented from \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1base_1_1Index_afe625ed4db692b26316b47f0315cf044}{pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+base.\+Index}}.

\index{\_union@{\_union}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{\_union()}{\_union()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_aa30889f4af9d13612a191b7480a590d5} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+\_\+union (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{other}{, }\item[{}]{sort}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Specific union logic should go here. In subclasses, union behavior
should be overwritten here rather than in `self.union`.

Parameters
----------
other : Index or array-like
sort : False or None, default False
    Whether to sort the resulting index.

    * True : sort the result
    * False : do not sort the result.
    * None : sort the result, except when `self` and `other` are equal
      or when the values cannot be compared.

Returns
-------
Index
\end{DoxyVerb}

pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+append (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{other}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Append a collection of Index options together.

Parameters
----------
other : Index or list/tuple of indices

Returns
-------
Index
    The combined index.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([['a'], ['b']])
>>> mi
MultiIndex([('a', 'b')],
           )
>>> mi.append(mi)
MultiIndex([('a', 'b'), ('a', 'b')],
           )
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ab7d4dca0372c9858df731ad2e0bbb6b4}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!argsort@{argsort}}
\index{argsort@{argsort}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{argsort()}{argsort()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ab7d4dca0372c9858df731ad2e0bbb6b4} 
 npt.\+NDArray\mbox{[}np.\+intp\mbox{]} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+argsort (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{args}{, }\item[{str }]{kwargs}{ = {\ttfamily "{}last"{}}, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{kwargs}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return the integer indices that would sort the index.

Parameters
----------
*args
    Passed to `numpy.ndarray.argsort`.
**kwargs
    Passed to `numpy.ndarray.argsort`.

Returns
-------
np.ndarray[np.intp]
    Integer indices that would sort the index if used as
    an indexer.

See Also
--------
numpy.argsort : Similar method for NumPy arrays.
Index.sort_values : Return sorted copy of Index.

Examples
--------
>>> idx = pd.Index(['b', 'a', 'd', 'c'])
>>> idx
Index(['b', 'a', 'd', 'c'], dtype='object')

>>> order = idx.argsort()
>>> order
array([1, 0, 3, 2])

>>> idx[order]
Index(['a', 'b', 'c', 'd'], dtype='object')
\end{DoxyVerb}

\index{astype@{astype}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{astype()}{astype()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ade759ef7ba0a8d23a9e76eda97fd3fe5} 
pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+astype (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{dtype}{, }\item[{bool }]{copy}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Create an Index with values cast to dtypes.

The class of a new Index is determined by dtype. When conversion is
impossible, a TypeError exception is raised.

Parameters
----------
dtype : numpy dtype or pandas type
    Note that any signed integer `dtype` is treated as ``'int64'``,
    and any unsigned integer `dtype` is treated as ``'uint64'``,
    regardless of the size.
copy : bool, default True
    By default, astype always returns a newly allocated object.
    If copy is set to False and internal requirements on dtype are
    satisfied, the original data is used to create a new Index
    or the original Index is returned.

Returns
-------
Index
    Index with values cast to specified dtype.

Examples
--------
>>> idx = pd.Index([1, 2, 3])
>>> idx
Index([1, 2, 3], dtype='int64')
>>> idx.astype('float')
Index([1.0, 2.0, 3.0], dtype='float64')
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented from \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1base_1_1Index_a248f0c2a5875cdd3e5ab34220dc34950}{pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+base.\+Index}}.

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ac3a7c7b154f9bfaf5ff79b51271e348d}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!copy@{copy}}
\index{copy@{copy}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{copy()}{copy()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ac3a7c7b154f9bfaf5ff79b51271e348d} 
 Self pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+copy (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{names}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{bool }]{deep}{ = {\ttfamily False}, }\item[{}]{name}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Make a copy of this object.

Names, dtype, levels and codes can be passed and will be set on new copy.

Parameters
----------
names : sequence, optional
deep : bool, default False
name : Label
    Kept for compatibility with 1-dimensional Index. Should not be used.

Returns
-------
MultiIndex

Notes
-----
In most cases, there should be no functional difference from using
``deep``, but if ``deep`` is passed it will attempt to deepcopy.
This could be potentially expensive on large MultiIndex objects.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([['a'], ['b'], ['c']])
>>> mi
MultiIndex([('a', 'b', 'c')],
           )
>>> mi.copy()
MultiIndex([('a', 'b', 'c')],
           )
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented from \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1base_1_1Index_a530f602c473a43194a45d49dbf1f62e0}{pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+base.\+Index}}.

 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+drop (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{codes}{, }\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1base_1_1Index}{Index}} \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} np.\+ndarray \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} Iterable\mbox{[}Hashable\mbox{]} \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} None }]{level}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{Ignore\+Raise }]{errors}{ = {\ttfamily "{}raise"{}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Make a new :class:`pandas.MultiIndex` with the passed list of codes deleted.

Parameters
----------
codes : array-like
    Must be a list of tuples when ``level`` is not specified.
level : int or level name, default None
errors : str, default 'raise'

Returns
-------
MultiIndex

Examples
--------
>>> idx = pd.MultiIndex.from_product([(0, 1, 2), ('green', 'purple')],
...                                  names=["number", "color"])
>>> idx
MultiIndex([(0,  'green'),
            (0, 'purple'),
            (1,  'green'),
            (1, 'purple'),
            (2,  'green'),
            (2, 'purple')],
           names=['number', 'color'])
>>> idx.drop([(1, 'green'), (2, 'purple')])
MultiIndex([(0,  'green'),
            (0, 'purple'),
            (1, 'purple'),
            (2,  'green')],
           names=['number', 'color'])

We can also drop from a specific level.

>>> idx.drop('green', level='color')
MultiIndex([(0, 'purple'),
            (1, 'purple'),
            (2, 'purple')],
           names=['number', 'color'])

>>> idx.drop([1, 2], level=0)
MultiIndex([(0,  'green'),
            (0, 'purple')],
           names=['number', 'color'])
\end{DoxyVerb}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{dropna()}{dropna()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a00de9adf230e2e7077cd878655ed033e} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+dropna (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{Any\+All }]{how}{ = {\ttfamily "{}any"{}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return Index without NA/NaN values.

Parameters
----------
how : {'any', 'all'}, default 'any'
    If the Index is a MultiIndex, drop the value when any or all levels
    are NaN.

Returns
-------
Index

Examples
--------
>>> idx = pd.Index([1, np.nan, 3])
>>> idx.dropna()
Index([1.0, 3.0], dtype='float64')
\end{DoxyVerb}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{dtypes()}{dtypes()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a3ea689f6d5cb442d9b2fe2530f720553} 
 Series pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+dtypes (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return the dtypes as a Series for the underlying MultiIndex.

Examples
--------
>>> idx = pd.MultiIndex.from_product([(0, 1, 2), ('green', 'purple')],
...                                  names=['number', 'color'])
>>> idx
MultiIndex([(0,  'green'),
            (0, 'purple'),
            (1,  'green'),
            (1, 'purple'),
            (2,  'green'),
            (2, 'purple')],
           names=['number', 'color'])
>>> idx.dtypes
number     int64
color     object
dtype: object
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a89d330fdc652b410302a7fd02546c984}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!duplicated@{duplicated}}
\index{duplicated@{duplicated}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{duplicated()}{duplicated()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a89d330fdc652b410302a7fd02546c984} 
 npt.\+NDArray\mbox{[}np.\+bool\+\_\+\mbox{]} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+duplicated (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{Drop\+Keep }]{keep}{ = {\ttfamily "{}first"{}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Indicate duplicate index values.

Duplicated values are indicated as ``True`` values in the resulting
array. Either all duplicates, all except the first, or all except the
last occurrence of duplicates can be indicated.

Parameters
----------
keep : {'first', 'last', False}, default 'first'
    The value or values in a set of duplicates to mark as missing.

    - 'first' : Mark duplicates as ``True`` except for the first
      occurrence.
    - 'last' : Mark duplicates as ``True`` except for the last
      occurrence.
    - ``False`` : Mark all duplicates as ``True``.

Returns
-------
np.ndarray[bool]

See Also
--------
Series.duplicated : Equivalent method on pandas.Series.
DataFrame.duplicated : Equivalent method on pandas.DataFrame.
Index.drop_duplicates : Remove duplicate values from Index.

Examples
--------
By default, for each set of duplicated values, the first occurrence is
set to False and all others to True:

>>> idx = pd.Index(['lama', 'cow', 'lama', 'beetle', 'lama'])
>>> idx.duplicated()
array([False, False,  True, False,  True])

which is equivalent to

>>> idx.duplicated(keep='first')
array([False, False,  True, False,  True])

By using 'last', the last occurrence of each set of duplicated values
is set on False and all others on True:

>>> idx.duplicated(keep='last')
array([ True, False,  True, False, False])

By setting keep on ``False``, all duplicates are True:

>>> idx.duplicated(keep=False)
array([ True, False,  True, False,  True])
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ab1cca07a58fbec6f4ed89b78e4365308}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!from\_arrays@{from\_arrays}}
\index{from\_arrays@{from\_arrays}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{from\_arrays()}{from\_arrays()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ab1cca07a58fbec6f4ed89b78e4365308} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+from\+\_\+arrays (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{cls}{, }\item[{}]{arrays}{, }\item[{int \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} None }]{sortorder}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{Sequence\mbox{[}Hashable\mbox{]} \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} Hashable \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} lib.\+No\+Default }]{names}{ = {\ttfamily lib.no\+\_\+default}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Convert arrays to MultiIndex.

Parameters
----------
arrays : list / sequence of array-likes
    Each array-like gives one level's value for each data point.
    len(arrays) is the number of levels.
sortorder : int or None
    Level of sortedness (must be lexicographically sorted by that
    level).
names : list / sequence of str, optional
    Names for the levels in the index.

Returns
-------
MultiIndex

See Also
--------
MultiIndex.from_tuples : Convert list of tuples to MultiIndex.
MultiIndex.from_product : Make a MultiIndex from cartesian product
                          of iterables.
MultiIndex.from_frame : Make a MultiIndex from a DataFrame.

Examples
--------
>>> arrays = [[1, 1, 2, 2], ['red', 'blue', 'red', 'blue']]
>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays(arrays, names=('number', 'color'))
MultiIndex([(1,  'red'),
            (1, 'blue'),
            (2,  'red'),
            (2, 'blue')],
           names=['number', 'color'])
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a9edea561b9fd2f2053cd49ecf6838148}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!from\_frame@{from\_frame}}
\index{from\_frame@{from\_frame}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{from\_frame()}{from\_frame()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a9edea561b9fd2f2053cd49ecf6838148} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+from\+\_\+frame (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{cls}{, }\item[{Data\+Frame}]{df}{, }\item[{int \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} None }]{sortorder}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{Sequence\mbox{[}Hashable\mbox{]} \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} Hashable \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} None }]{names}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Make a MultiIndex from a DataFrame.

Parameters
----------
df : DataFrame
    DataFrame to be converted to MultiIndex.
sortorder : int, optional
    Level of sortedness (must be lexicographically sorted by that
    level).
names : list-like, optional
    If no names are provided, use the column names, or tuple of column
    names if the columns is a MultiIndex. If a sequence, overwrite
    names with the given sequence.

Returns
-------
MultiIndex
    The MultiIndex representation of the given DataFrame.

See Also
--------
MultiIndex.from_arrays : Convert list of arrays to MultiIndex.
MultiIndex.from_tuples : Convert list of tuples to MultiIndex.
MultiIndex.from_product : Make a MultiIndex from cartesian product
                          of iterables.

Examples
--------
>>> df = pd.DataFrame([['HI', 'Temp'], ['HI', 'Precip'],
...                    ['NJ', 'Temp'], ['NJ', 'Precip']],
...                   columns=['a', 'b'])
>>> df
      a       b
0    HI    Temp
1    HI  Precip
2    NJ    Temp
3    NJ  Precip

>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_frame(df)
MultiIndex([('HI',   'Temp'),
            ('HI', 'Precip'),
            ('NJ',   'Temp'),
            ('NJ', 'Precip')],
           names=['a', 'b'])

Using explicit names, instead of the column names

>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_frame(df, names=['state', 'observation'])
MultiIndex([('HI',   'Temp'),
            ('HI', 'Precip'),
            ('NJ',   'Temp'),
            ('NJ', 'Precip')],
           names=['state', 'observation'])
\end{DoxyVerb}

 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+from\+\_\+product (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{cls}{, }\item[{Sequence\mbox{[}Iterable\mbox{[}Hashable\mbox{]}\mbox{]}}]{iterables}{, }\item[{int \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} None }]{sortorder}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{Sequence\mbox{[}Hashable\mbox{]} \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} Hashable \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} lib.\+No\+Default }]{names}{ = {\ttfamily lib.no\+\_\+default}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Make a MultiIndex from the cartesian product of multiple iterables.

Parameters
----------
iterables : list / sequence of iterables
    Each iterable has unique labels for each level of the index.
sortorder : int or None
    Level of sortedness (must be lexicographically sorted by that
    level).
names : list / sequence of str, optional
    Names for the levels in the index.
    If not explicitly provided, names will be inferred from the
    elements of iterables if an element has a name attribute.

Returns
-------
MultiIndex

See Also
--------
MultiIndex.from_arrays : Convert list of arrays to MultiIndex.
MultiIndex.from_tuples : Convert list of tuples to MultiIndex.
MultiIndex.from_frame : Make a MultiIndex from a DataFrame.

Examples
--------
>>> numbers = [0, 1, 2]
>>> colors = ['green', 'purple']
>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_product([numbers, colors],
...                            names=['number', 'color'])
MultiIndex([(0,  'green'),
            (0, 'purple'),
            (1,  'green'),
            (1, 'purple'),
            (2,  'green'),
            (2, 'purple')],
           names=['number', 'color'])
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a94953631ca8377e1c7973a90239e511f}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!get\_level\_values@{get\_level\_values}}
\index{get\_level\_values@{get\_level\_values}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_level\_values()}{get\_level\_values()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a94953631ca8377e1c7973a90239e511f} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1base_1_1Index}{Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+get\+\_\+level\+\_\+values (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{level}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return vector of label values for requested level.

Length of returned vector is equal to the length of the index.

Parameters
----------
level : int or str
    ``level`` is either the integer position of the level in the
    MultiIndex, or the name of the level.

Returns
-------
Index
    Values is a level of this MultiIndex converted to
    a single :class:`Index` (or subclass thereof).

Notes
-----
If the level contains missing values, the result may be casted to
``float`` with missing values specified as ``NaN``. This is because
the level is converted to a regular ``Index``.

Examples
--------
Create a MultiIndex:

>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays((list('abc'), list('def')))
>>> mi.names = ['level_1', 'level_2']

Get level values by supplying level as either integer or name:

>>> mi.get_level_values(0)
Index(['a', 'b', 'c'], dtype='object', name='level_1')
>>> mi.get_level_values('level_2')
Index(['d', 'e', 'f'], dtype='object', name='level_2')

If a level contains missing values, the return type of the level
may be cast to ``float``.

>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([[1, None, 2], [3, 4, 5]]).dtypes
level_0    int64
level_1    int64
dtype: object
>>> pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([[1, None, 2], [3, 4, 5]]).get_level_values(0)
Index([1.0, nan, 2.0], dtype='float64')
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented from \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1base_1_1Index}{pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+base.\+Index}}.

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_aa47592ee63f7c5211e56a9b044022ead}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!get\_loc@{get\_loc}}
\index{get\_loc@{get\_loc}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_loc()}{get\_loc()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_aa47592ee63f7c5211e56a9b044022ead} 
pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+get\+\_\+loc (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{key}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Get location for a label or a tuple of labels.

The location is returned as an integer/slice or boolean
mask.

Parameters
----------
key : label or tuple of labels (one for each level)

Returns
-------
int, slice object or boolean mask
    If the key is past the lexsort depth, the return may be a
    boolean mask array, otherwise it is always a slice or int.

See Also
--------
Index.get_loc : The get_loc method for (single-level) index.
MultiIndex.slice_locs : Get slice location given start label(s) and
                        end label(s).
MultiIndex.get_locs : Get location for a label/slice/list/mask or a
                      sequence of such.

Notes
-----
The key cannot be a slice, list of same-level labels, a boolean mask,
or a sequence of such. If you want to use those, use
:meth:`MultiIndex.get_locs` instead.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([list('abb'), list('def')])

>>> mi.get_loc('b')
slice(1, 3, None)

>>> mi.get_loc(('b', 'e'))
1
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a515ff4df91edbdbdd046dfec4b5d07d0}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!get\_loc\_level@{get\_loc\_level}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_loc\_level()}{get\_loc\_level()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a515ff4df91edbdbdd046dfec4b5d07d0} 
pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+get\+\_\+loc\+\_\+level (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{key}{, }\item[{Index\+Label }]{level}{ = {\ttfamily 0}, }\item[{bool }]{drop\+\_\+level}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Get location and sliced index for requested label(s)/level(s).

Parameters
----------
key : label or sequence of labels
level : int/level name or list thereof, optional
drop_level : bool, default True
    If ``False``, the resulting index will not drop any level.

Returns
-------
tuple
    A 2-tuple where the elements :

    Element 0: int, slice object or boolean array.

    Element 1: The resulting sliced multiindex/index. If the key
    contains all levels, this will be ``None``.

See Also
--------
MultiIndex.get_loc  : Get location for a label or a tuple of labels.
MultiIndex.get_locs : Get location for a label/slice/list/mask or a
                      sequence of such.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([list('abb'), list('def')],
...                                names=['A', 'B'])

>>> mi.get_loc_level('b')
(slice(1, 3, None), Index(['e', 'f'], dtype='object', name='B'))

>>> mi.get_loc_level('e', level='B')
(array([False,  True, False]), Index(['b'], dtype='object', name='A'))

>>> mi.get_loc_level(['b', 'e'])
(1, None)
\end{DoxyVerb}

 npt.\+NDArray\mbox{[}np.\+intp\mbox{]} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+get\+\_\+locs (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{seq}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Get location for a sequence of labels.

Parameters
----------
seq : label, slice, list, mask or a sequence of such
   You should use one of the above for each level.
   If a level should not be used, set it to ``slice(None)``.

Returns
-------
numpy.ndarray
    NumPy array of integers suitable for passing to iloc.

MultiIndex.get_loc : Get location for a label or a tuple of labels.

                        end label(s).

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([list('abb'), list('def')])

>>> mi.get_locs('b')  # doctest: +SKIP
array([1, 2], dtype=int64)

>>> mi.get_locs([slice(None), ['e', 'f']])  # doctest: +SKIP
array([1, 2], dtype=int64)

>>> mi.get_locs([[True, False, True], slice('e', 'f')])  # doctest: +SKIP
array([2], dtype=int64)
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a370cbee88acd659829f06aba75fa194c}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!get\_slice\_bound@{get\_slice\_bound}}
\index{get\_slice\_bound@{get\_slice\_bound}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{get\_slice\_bound()}{get\_slice\_bound()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a370cbee88acd659829f06aba75fa194c} 
 int pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+get\+\_\+slice\+\_\+bound (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{Hashable \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} Sequence\mbox{[}Hashable\mbox{]}}]{label}{, }\item[{Literal\mbox{[}"{}left"{}, "{}right"{}\mbox{]}}]{side}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}For an ordered MultiIndex, compute slice bound
that corresponds to given label.

Returns leftmost (one-past-the-rightmost if `side=='right') position
of given label.

Parameters
----------
label : object or tuple of objects
side : {'left', 'right'}

Returns
-------
int
    Index of label.

Notes
-----
This method only works if level 0 index of the MultiIndex is lexsorted.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([list('abbc'), list('gefd')])

Get the locations from the leftmost 'b' in the first level
until the end of the multiindex:

>>> mi.get_slice_bound('b', side="left")
1

Like above, but if you get the locations from the rightmost
'b' in the first level and 'f' in the second level:

>>> mi.get_slice_bound(('b','f'), side="right")
3

See Also
--------
MultiIndex.get_loc : Get location for a label or a tuple of labels.
MultiIndex.get_locs : Get location for a label/slice/list/mask or a
                      sequence of such.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_affa2b4562917b715115340bc3e15951b}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!isin@{isin}}
\index{isin@{isin}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{isin()}{isin()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_affa2b4562917b715115340bc3e15951b} 
 npt.\+NDArray\mbox{[}np.\+bool\+\_\+\mbox{]} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+isin (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{values}{, }\item[{}]{level}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return a boolean array where the index values are in `values`.

Compute boolean array of whether each index value is found in the
passed set of values. The length of the returned boolean array matches
the length of the index.

Parameters
----------
values : set or list-like
    Sought values.
level : str or int, optional
    Name or position of the index level to use (if the index is a
    `MultiIndex`).

Returns
-------
np.ndarray[bool]
    NumPy array of boolean values.

See Also
--------
Series.isin : Same for Series.
DataFrame.isin : Same method for DataFrames.

Notes
-----
In the case of `MultiIndex` you must either specify `values` as a
list-like object containing tuples that are the same length as the
number of levels, or specify `level`. Otherwise it will raise a
``ValueError``.

If `level` is specified:

- if it is the name of one *and only one* index level, use that level;
- otherwise it should be a number indicating level position.

Examples
--------
>>> idx = pd.Index([1,2,3])
>>> idx
Index([1, 2, 3], dtype='int64')

Check whether each index value in a list of values.

>>> idx.isin([1, 4])
array([ True, False, False])

>>> midx = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([[1,2,3],
...                                  ['red', 'blue', 'green']],
...                                  names=('number', 'color'))
>>> midx
MultiIndex([(1,   'red'),
            (2,  'blue'),
            (3, 'green')],
           names=['number', 'color'])

Check whether the strings in the 'color' level of the MultiIndex
are in a list of colors.

>>> midx.isin(['red', 'orange', 'yellow'], level='color')
array([ True, False, False])

To check across the levels of a MultiIndex, pass a list of tuples:

>>> midx.isin([(1, 'red'), (3, 'red')])
array([ True, False, False])
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Reimplemented from \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1base_1_1Index_ad4e4887bf57bd655762834e00c60383f}{pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+base.\+Index}}.



Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{multi_8py_source_l04006}{4006}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{multi_8py_source}{multi.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a412b28d222a7a8b93a9335e3e40b7da2}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!levels@{levels}}
\index{levels@{levels}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{levels()}{levels()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a412b28d222a7a8b93a9335e3e40b7da2} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1frozen_1_1FrozenList}{Frozen\+List}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+levels (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Levels of the MultiIndex.

Levels refer to the different hierarchical levels or layers in a MultiIndex.
In a MultiIndex, each level represents a distinct dimension or category of
the index.

To access the levels, you can use the levels attribute of the MultiIndex,
which returns a tuple of Index objects. Each Index object represents a
level in the MultiIndex and contains the unique values found in that
specific level.

If a MultiIndex is created with levels A, B, C, and the DataFrame using
it filters out all rows of the level C, MultiIndex.levels will still
return A, B, C.

Examples
--------
>>> index = pd.MultiIndex.from_product([['mammal'],
...                                     ('goat', 'human', 'cat', 'dog')],
...                                    names=['Category', 'Animals'])
>>> leg_num = pd.DataFrame(data=(4, 2, 4, 4), index=index, columns=['Legs'])
>>> leg_num
                  Legs
Category Animals
mammal   goat        4
         human       2
         cat         4
         dog         4

>>> leg_num.index.levels
FrozenList([['mammal'], ['cat', 'dog', 'goat', 'human']])

MultiIndex levels will not change even if the DataFrame using the MultiIndex
does not contain all them anymore.
See how "human" is not in the DataFrame, but it is still in levels:

>>> large_leg_num = leg_num[leg_num.Legs > 2]
>>> large_leg_num
                  Legs
Category Animals
mammal   goat        4
         cat         4
         dog         4

>>> large_leg_num.index.levels
FrozenList([['mammal'], ['cat', 'dog', 'goat', 'human']])
\end{DoxyVerb}
 

Definition at line \mbox{\hyperlink{multi_8py_source_l00846}{846}} of file \mbox{\hyperlink{multi_8py_source}{multi.\+py}}.

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a5cb8bb8e6c601653cf8197ea334be899}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!remove\_unused\_levels@{remove\_unused\_levels}}
\index{remove\_unused\_levels@{remove\_unused\_levels}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{remove\_unused\_levels()}{remove\_unused\_levels()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a5cb8bb8e6c601653cf8197ea334be899} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+remove\+\_\+unused\+\_\+levels (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Create new MultiIndex from current that removes unused levels.

Unused level(s) means levels that are not expressed in the
labels. The resulting MultiIndex will have the same outward
appearance, meaning the same .values and ordering. It will
also be .equals() to the original.

Returns
-------
MultiIndex

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_product([range(2), list('ab')])
>>> mi
MultiIndex([(0, 'a'),
            (0, 'b'),
            (1, 'a'),
            (1, 'b')],
           )

>>> mi[2:]
MultiIndex([(1, 'a'),
            (1, 'b')],
           )

The 0 from the first level is not represented
and can be removed

>>> mi2 = mi[2:].remove_unused_levels()
>>> mi2.levels
FrozenList([[1], ['a', 'b']])
\end{DoxyVerb}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{reorder\_levels()}{reorder\_levels()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a4216539497b0533643bd665621d3a22e} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+reorder\+\_\+levels (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{order}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Rearrange levels using input order. May not drop or duplicate levels.

Parameters
----------
order : list of int or list of str
    List representing new level order. Reference level by number
    (position) or by key (label).

Returns
-------
MultiIndex

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([[1, 2], [3, 4]], names=['x', 'y'])
>>> mi
MultiIndex([(1, 3),
            (2, 4)],
           names=['x', 'y'])

>>> mi.reorder_levels(order=[1, 0])
MultiIndex([(3, 1),
            (4, 2)],
           names=['y', 'x'])

>>> mi.reorder_levels(order=['y', 'x'])
MultiIndex([(3, 1),
            (4, 2)],
           names=['y', 'x'])
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ad73fb55f12499a3bce3109aa0509896e}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!set\_codes@{set\_codes}}
\index{set\_codes@{set\_codes}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{set\_codes()}{set\_codes()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ad73fb55f12499a3bce3109aa0509896e} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+set\+\_\+codes (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{codes}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{}]{level}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{bool }]{verify\+\_\+integrity}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Set new codes on MultiIndex. Defaults to returning new index.

Parameters
----------
codes : sequence or list of sequence
    New codes to apply.
level : int, level name, or sequence of int/level names (default None)
    Level(s) to set (None for all levels).
verify_integrity : bool, default True
    If True, checks that levels and codes are compatible.

Returns
-------
new index (of same type and class...etc) or None
    The same type as the caller or None if ``inplace=True``.

Examples
--------
>>> idx = pd.MultiIndex.from_tuples(
...     [(1, "one"), (1, "two"), (2, "one"), (2, "two")], names=["foo", "bar"]
... )
>>> idx
MultiIndex([(1, 'one'),
    (1, 'two'),
    (2, 'one'),
    (2, 'two')],
   names=['foo', 'bar'])

>>> idx.set_codes([[1, 0, 1, 0], [0, 0, 1, 1]])
MultiIndex([(2, 'one'),
            (1, 'one'),
            (2, 'two'),
            (1, 'two')],
           names=['foo', 'bar'])
>>> idx.set_codes([1, 0, 1, 0], level=0)
MultiIndex([(2, 'one'),
            (1, 'two'),
            (2, 'one'),
            (1, 'two')],
           names=['foo', 'bar'])
>>> idx.set_codes([0, 0, 1, 1], level='bar')
MultiIndex([(1, 'one'),
            (1, 'one'),
            (2, 'two'),
            (2, 'two')],
           names=['foo', 'bar'])
>>> idx.set_codes([[1, 0, 1, 0], [0, 0, 1, 1]], level=[0, 1])
MultiIndex([(2, 'one'),
            (1, 'one'),
            (2, 'two'),
            (1, 'two')],
           names=['foo', 'bar'])
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a65a0254785dc61eba1dd7cd86ba804e5}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!set\_levels@{set\_levels}}
\index{set\_levels@{set\_levels}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{set\_levels()}{set\_levels()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a65a0254785dc61eba1dd7cd86ba804e5} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+set\+\_\+levels (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{levels}{, }\item[{\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{}{, }\item[{}]{level}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{bool }]{verify\+\_\+integrity}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Set new levels on MultiIndex. Defaults to returning new index.

Parameters
----------
levels : sequence or list of sequence
    New level(s) to apply.
level : int, level name, or sequence of int/level names (default None)
    Level(s) to set (None for all levels).
verify_integrity : bool, default True
    If True, checks that levels and codes are compatible.

Returns
-------
MultiIndex

Examples
--------
>>> idx = pd.MultiIndex.from_tuples(
...     [
...         (1, "one"),
...         (1, "two"),
...         (2, "one"),
...         (2, "two"),
...         (3, "one"),
...         (3, "two")
...     ],
...     names=["foo", "bar"]
... )
>>> idx
MultiIndex([(1, 'one'),
    (1, 'two'),
    (2, 'one'),
    (2, 'two'),
    (3, 'one'),
    (3, 'two')],
   names=['foo', 'bar'])

>>> idx.set_levels([['a', 'b', 'c'], [1, 2]])
MultiIndex([('a', 1),
            ('a', 2),
            ('b', 1),
            ('b', 2),
            ('c', 1),
            ('c', 2)],
           names=['foo', 'bar'])
>>> idx.set_levels(['a', 'b', 'c'], level=0)
MultiIndex([('a', 'one'),
            ('a', 'two'),
            ('b', 'one'),
            ('b', 'two'),
            ('c', 'one'),
            ('c', 'two')],
           names=['foo', 'bar'])
>>> idx.set_levels(['a', 'b'], level='bar')
MultiIndex([(1, 'a'),
            (1, 'b'),
            (2, 'a'),
            (2, 'b'),
            (3, 'a'),
            (3, 'b')],
           names=['foo', 'bar'])

If any of the levels passed to ``set_levels()`` exceeds the
existing length, all of the values from that argument will
be stored in the MultiIndex levels, though the values will
be truncated in the MultiIndex output.

>>> idx.set_levels([['a', 'b', 'c'], [1, 2, 3, 4]], level=[0, 1])
MultiIndex([('a', 1),
    ('a', 2),
    ('b', 1),
    ('b', 2),
    ('c', 1),
    ('c', 2)],
   names=['foo', 'bar'])
>>> idx.set_levels([['a', 'b', 'c'], [1, 2, 3, 4]], level=[0, 1]).levels
FrozenList([['a', 'b', 'c'], [1, 2, 3, 4]])
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a05c91938bc58c129cb10de8c684ce9e0}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!slice\_locs@{slice\_locs}}
\index{slice\_locs@{slice\_locs}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{slice\_locs()}{slice\_locs()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a05c91938bc58c129cb10de8c684ce9e0} 
 tuple\mbox{[}int, int\mbox{]} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+slice\+\_\+locs (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{start}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{end}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{step}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}For an ordered MultiIndex, compute the slice locations for input
labels.

The input labels can be tuples representing partial levels, e.g. for a
MultiIndex with 3 levels, you can pass a single value (corresponding to
the first level), or a 1-, 2-, or 3-tuple.

Parameters
----------
start : label or tuple, default None
    If None, defaults to the beginning
end : label or tuple
    If None, defaults to the end
step : int or None
    Slice step

Returns
-------
(start, end) : (int, int)

Notes
-----
This method only works if the MultiIndex is properly lexsorted. So,
if only the first 2 levels of a 3-level MultiIndex are lexsorted,
you can only pass two levels to ``.slice_locs``.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([list('abbd'), list('deff')],
...                                names=['A', 'B'])

Get the slice locations from the beginning of 'b' in the first level
until the end of the multiindex:

>>> mi.slice_locs(start='b')
(1, 4)

Like above, but stop at the end of 'b' in the first level and 'f' in
the second level:

>>> mi.slice_locs(start='b', end=('b', 'f'))
(1, 3)

See Also
--------
MultiIndex.get_loc : Get location for a label or a tuple of labels.
MultiIndex.get_locs : Get location for a label/slice/list/mask or a
                      sequence of such.
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_afbb51f0b7f7373fc404450a675e34e38}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!sortlevel@{sortlevel}}
\index{sortlevel@{sortlevel}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{sortlevel()}{sortlevel()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_afbb51f0b7f7373fc404450a675e34e38} 
 tuple\mbox{[}\mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}}, npt.\+NDArray\mbox{[}np.\+intp\mbox{]}\mbox{]} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+sortlevel (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{Index\+Label }]{level}{ = {\ttfamily 0}, }\item[{bool \texorpdfstring{$\vert$}{|} list\mbox{[}bool\mbox{]} }]{ascending}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}, }\item[{bool }]{sort\+\_\+remaining}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}, }\item[{str }]{na\+\_\+position}{ = {\ttfamily "{}first"{}}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Sort MultiIndex at the requested level.

The result will respect the original ordering of the associated
factor at that level.

Parameters
----------
level : list-like, int or str, default 0
    If a string is given, must be a name of the level.
    If list-like must be names or ints of levels.
ascending : bool, default True
    False to sort in descending order.
    Can also be a list to specify a directed ordering.
sort_remaining : sort by the remaining levels after level
na_position : {'first' or 'last'}, default 'first'
    Argument 'first' puts NaNs at the beginning, 'last' puts NaNs at
    the end.

    .. versionadded:: 2.1.0

Returns
-------
sorted_index : pd.MultiIndex
    Resulting index.
indexer : np.ndarray[np.intp]
    Indices of output values in original index.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([[0, 0], [2, 1]])
>>> mi
MultiIndex([(0, 2),
            (0, 1)],
           )

>>> mi.sortlevel()
(MultiIndex([(0, 1),
            (0, 2)],
           ), array([1, 0]))

>>> mi.sortlevel(sort_remaining=False)
(MultiIndex([(0, 2),
            (0, 1)],
           ), array([0, 1]))

>>> mi.sortlevel(1)
(MultiIndex([(0, 1),
            (0, 2)],
           ), array([1, 0]))

>>> mi.sortlevel(1, ascending=False)
(MultiIndex([(0, 2),
            (0, 1)],
           ), array([0, 1]))
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a48ac98db30fdc578c9d5b82bdd0350c9}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!swaplevel@{swaplevel}}
\index{swaplevel@{swaplevel}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{swaplevel()}{swaplevel()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a48ac98db30fdc578c9d5b82bdd0350c9} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+swaplevel (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{i}{ = {\ttfamily -\/2}, }\item[{}]{j}{ = {\ttfamily -\/1}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Swap level i with level j.

Calling this method does not change the ordering of the values.

Parameters
----------
i : int, str, default -2
    First level of index to be swapped. Can pass level name as string.
    Type of parameters can be mixed.
j : int, str, default -1
    Second level of index to be swapped. Can pass level name as string.
    Type of parameters can be mixed.

Returns
-------
MultiIndex
    A new MultiIndex.

See Also
--------
Series.swaplevel : Swap levels i and j in a MultiIndex.
DataFrame.swaplevel : Swap levels i and j in a MultiIndex on a
    particular axis.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex(levels=[['a', 'b'], ['bb', 'aa']],
...                    codes=[[0, 0, 1, 1], [0, 1, 0, 1]])
>>> mi
MultiIndex([('a', 'bb'),
            ('a', 'aa'),
            ('b', 'bb'),
            ('b', 'aa')],
           )
>>> mi.swaplevel(0, 1)
MultiIndex([('bb', 'a'),
            ('aa', 'a'),
            ('bb', 'b'),
            ('aa', 'b')],
           )
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a410e956d736f5ba47764a2b45b61a3ce}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!to\_flat\_index@{to\_flat\_index}}
\index{to\_flat\_index@{to\_flat\_index}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{to\_flat\_index()}{to\_flat\_index()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_a410e956d736f5ba47764a2b45b61a3ce} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1base_1_1Index}{Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+to\+\_\+flat\+\_\+index (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Convert a MultiIndex to an Index of Tuples containing the level values.

Returns
-------
pd.Index
    Index with the MultiIndex data represented in Tuples.

See Also
--------
MultiIndex.from_tuples : Convert flat index back to MultiIndex.

Notes
-----
This method will simply return the caller if called by anything other
than a MultiIndex.

Examples
--------
>>> index = pd.MultiIndex.from_product(
...     [['foo', 'bar'], ['baz', 'qux']],
...     names=['a', 'b'])
>>> index.to_flat_index()
Index([('foo', 'baz'), ('foo', 'qux'),
       ('bar', 'baz'), ('bar', 'qux')],
      dtype='object')
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_aa0dd51a4387d687a5673fb95a2359769}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!to\_frame@{to\_frame}}
\index{to\_frame@{to\_frame}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{to\_frame()}{to\_frame()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_aa0dd51a4387d687a5673fb95a2359769} 
 Data\+Frame pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+to\+\_\+frame (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{bool }]{index}{ = {\ttfamily \mbox{\hyperlink{classTrue}{True}}}, }\item[{}]{name}{ = {\ttfamily lib.no\+\_\+default}, }\item[{bool }]{allow\+\_\+duplicates}{ = {\ttfamily False}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Create a DataFrame with the levels of the MultiIndex as columns.

Column ordering is determined by the DataFrame constructor with data as
a dict.

Parameters
----------
index : bool, default True
    Set the index of the returned DataFrame as the original MultiIndex.

name : list / sequence of str, optional
    The passed names should substitute index level names.

allow_duplicates : bool, optional default False
    Allow duplicate column labels to be created.

    .. versionadded:: 1.5.0

Returns
-------
DataFrame

See Also
--------
DataFrame : Two-dimensional, size-mutable, potentially heterogeneous
    tabular data.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([['a', 'b'], ['c', 'd']])
>>> mi
MultiIndex([('a', 'c'),
            ('b', 'd')],
           )

>>> df = mi.to_frame()
>>> df
     0  1
a c  a  c
b d  b  d

>>> df = mi.to_frame(index=False)
>>> df
   0  1
0  a  c
1  b  d

>>> df = mi.to_frame(name=['x', 'y'])
>>> df
     x  y
a c  a  c
b d  b  d
\end{DoxyVerb}

\Hypertarget{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_aac3dda715c44709b23f4260287057aeb}\index{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}!truncate@{truncate}}
\index{truncate@{truncate}!pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex@{pandas.core.indexes.multi.MultiIndex}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{truncate()}{truncate()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_aac3dda715c44709b23f4260287057aeb} 
 \mbox{\hyperlink{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex}{Multi\+Index}} pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+truncate (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{before}{ = {\ttfamily None}, }\item[{}]{after}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Slice index between two labels / tuples, return new MultiIndex.

Parameters
----------
before : label or tuple, can be partial. Default None
    None defaults to start.
after : label or tuple, can be partial. Default None
    None defaults to end.

Returns
-------
MultiIndex
    The truncated MultiIndex.

Examples
--------
>>> mi = pd.MultiIndex.from_arrays([['a', 'b', 'c'], ['x', 'y', 'z']])
>>> mi
MultiIndex([('a', 'x'), ('b', 'y'), ('c', 'z')],
           )
>>> mi.truncate(before='a', after='b')
MultiIndex([('a', 'x'), ('b', 'y')],
           )
\end{DoxyVerb}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{unique()}{unique()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{classpandas_1_1core_1_1indexes_1_1multi_1_1MultiIndex_ae61a80908267a0eaf218089d97615366} 
pandas.\+core.\+indexes.\+multi.\+Multi\+Index.\+unique (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{}]{self}{, }\item[{}]{level}{ = {\ttfamily None}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

\begin{DoxyVerb}Return unique values in the index.

Unique values are returned in order of appearance, this does NOT sort.

Parameters
----------
level : int or hashable, optional
    Only return values from specified level (for MultiIndex).
    If int, gets the level by integer position, else by level name.

Returns
-------
Index

See Also
--------
unique : Numpy array of unique values in that column.
Series.unique : Return unique values of Series object.

Examples
--------
>>> idx = pd.Index([1, 1, 2, 3, 3])
>>> idx.unique()
Index([1, 2, 3], dtype='int64')
\end{DoxyVerb}
